## CORRIGENDA

IN Gazette Notice No. 12641 of 2009, amend the  expression 'to be members of the Board of Directors of Athi Water Services Board, with effect from 27th November, 2009' to read 'to be members of the Board of Directors of Athi Water Services Board, for a period of three (3) years, with effect from 27th November, 2009'.

IN Gazette Notice No. 2045 of 2008, amend the deceased's place of  death  and  date  of  death  'Kenyatta  National  Hospital'  and  24th November,  2006'  to read 'Nairobi  West  Hospital'  and  9th  May, 2007', respectively.

IN Gazette notice No. 11078 of 2009, amend the Registrar's name printed as 'B. O. Ochieng' to read 'T. M. Mwangi'.

<span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 12941</span>
THE CUSTOMS AND EXCISE ACT

( Cap. 472)

APPOINTMENT

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by section 127 ( e ) (1) and 127 ( e ) (2) of the Customs and Excise Act, the Deputy Prime Minister and Minister for Finance appoints-

,

Josephine Kemunto Maangi - ( Chairperson) Isaac Opuya Litali, Peter Wambua Muthoka, Moses Buyuka Obonyo, Poloji Dickson Akalwa, Timothy Douglas Muchiri, to be members of the Appeals Tribunal for a period of three (3) years, with effect from 1st September, 2009.

Dated the 17th November, 2009.

<span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 12942</span>
## THE RESTRICTIVE TRADE PRACTICES, MONOPOLIES AND PRICE CONTROL ACT

( Cap. 504)

ACQUISITION OF A CONTROLLING INTEREST IN PACKET STREAM DATA NETWORKS LIMITED BY SAFARICOM LIMITED

IN  EXERCISE  of  the  powers  conferred  by  section  31  of  the Restrictive  Trade  Practises,  Monopolies  and  Price  Control  Act,  the Deputy Prime Minister  and  Minister  for  Finance  hereby    authorizes the acquistion of a controlling interest in Packet  Stream Data Networks Limited by Safaricom Limited.

Dated the 30th November, 2009.

UHURU KENYATTA, Deputy Prime Minister and Minister for Finance.

UHURU KENYATTA,

Deputy Prime Minister and Minister for Finance.

<span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 12943</span>
THE WATER ACT

( No. 8 of 2008)

## THE WATER SERVICES TRUST FUND

## APPOINTMENT

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by section 83 of the Water Act, 2002, the Minister for Water and Irrigation appoints-

MARTIN OLOO

to be a Trustee of the Water Services Trust Fund for a period of three (3)  years,  with  effect  from  27th  November,  2009,  and  revokes  the appointment of Carcy Francis Onyango*.

C. K. NGILU,

Minister for Water and Irrrigation.

*G.N. 12642/2009.

<span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 12944</span>
## THE KERIO VALLEY DEVELOPMENT AUTHORITY ACT ( Cap. 441)

## APPOINTMENT

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by section 4 (1) (h) of the Kerio Valley Development Authority Act, the Minister for Regional Development Authorities appoints-

## THE MANAGING DIRECTOR, KENYA ELECTRICITY GENERATING COMPANY LIMITED

to  be  a  member  of  the  Kerio  Valley  Development  Authority  for  a period of three (3) years, with effect from 1st December, 2009.

Dated the 26th November, 2009.

Minister for Regional Development Authorities.

CONSTANCE MWANDAWIRO KALELA

<span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 12946</span>
## THE CO-OPERATIVE SOCIETIES ACT

( Cap. 490)

EXEMPTION ORDER

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by section 92 (1) of the Co-operative  Societies  Act,  2004,  the  Minister  for  Co-operative Development and Marketing exempts-

KENYA CO-OPERATIVE COFFEE EXPORTERS LIMITED, CS/NO. 12173 from the provisons of section 28 (1) of the Act.

Dated the 2nd December, 2009.

Minister for Co-operative Development and Marketing.

<span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 12947</span>
## THE CRIMINAL PROCEDURE CODE

( Cap. 75)

APPOINTMENT

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by section 85 ( 2 )  of  the Criminal  Procedure  Code  and  pursuant  to  section  260  of  the  Local Government Act (Cap. 265), the Attorney-General appoints-

DAVID MAENDE OKELO

to be a public prosecutor for the purposes of all cases arising under the Local Government Act, or under any by-law made by the Municipal Council of Busia, whether under that Act or otherwise.

Dated the 30th November, 2009.

<span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 12948</span>
## TASKFORCE ON THE IMPLEMENTATION OF THE SEXUAL OFFENCES ACT, 2006

EXTENSION OF PERIOD OF APPOINTMENT

IT IS notified for general information of the public that the period of appointment of the Task Force on the Implementation of the Sexual Offences  Act,  2006,  contained  in  Gazette  Notice  No.  2155  of  2007 has been further extended to the 31st December, 2010.

Dated the 30th November, 2009.

F. O. GUMO,

F. O. GUMO,

J. W. N. NYAGAH,

S. A. WAKO, Attorney General.

S. A. WAKO, Attorney General.

| GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 12949 THE NATIONAL TOURISM CRISIS MANAGEMENT COMMITTEE APPOINTMENT IT IS notified for information of the public that the Minister for Tourism has appointed a Committee to be known as the National Tourism Crisis Management Committee. The Committee shall comprise of the following persons: Eunice K. Miima -( Chairman),                        | Further, the Ministry has established a (Crisis Response Committee drawn from the Management Committee comprising the following persons: Kipkorir Lagat, Jake Grieves-Cook, Mike Macharia, Fred Kaigua, Esther Kamweru. The Crisis Response Team shall- (a) receive and collect information on any actual or potential risk; (b) evaluate and assess the available information with regard to the significance and magnitude of the actual and potential risk; (c) manage the communication and dissemination of information to all institutions in timely manner; and (d) assist with co-ordination, monitoring and re-evaluation of the risk response efforts. The Committee shall work closely with the National Disaster Management-Co-ordination Centre and other relevant institutions in the management of all crisis situations. In the performance of its function, the Committee may co-opt additional expertise as may be required from time to time, specialized aspects of its terms of reference. The secretariat of the Committee shall be based at:   |

## THE REGISTRATION OF TITLES ACT

( Cap. 281, section 71)

## ISSUE OF A PROVISIONAL CERTIFICATE

WHEREAS Dominic  Thuita  Samson  Gathege,  of  P.O.  Box  69887, Nairobi in the Republic of Kenya, is  the registered proprietor of that piece  of  land  known  as  L.R.  No.  209/1249/2,  situate  in  the  city  of Nairobi, by virtue of a grant registered as I.R. 77186/1, and whereas sufficient  evidence  has  been  adduced  to  show  that  the  said  grant issued thereof has been lost, notice is given that after the expiration of ninety  (90)  days  from  the  date  hereof,  I  shall  issue  a  provisional certificate of title provided that no objection has been received within that period.

Dated the 4th December, 2009.

G. G. GACHIHI, Registrar of Titles, Nairobi.

<span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 12952</span>

## THE COMPANIES ACT ( Cap . 486)

## PAYMENT OF DIVIDEND

NOTICE  is  given  that  the  Deposit  Protection  Fund  Board,  in exercise of the powers under rule 107 of the Companies (Winding-up) rules,  shall  with  effect  from  14th  December,  2009,  appoint  the liquidation  agent  of  Meridien  Biao  Bank  Limited  (in  liquidation)  to pay a second dividend to all depositors and creditors who have proved their debts.

Payments will be made during working days (Monday to Friday) at  the  institution's  offices  on  the  2nd  Floor  of  Marshalls  House, Harambee Avenue, Nairobi, between the hours of 9.00 a.m. and 4.00 p.m.

Claims  for  the  second  dividend  should  be  made  within  a  period not exceeding one (1) year effective 14th December, 2009. Depositors and other creditors who have already lodged their claims automatically  qualify  for  the  second  dividend  and  need  not  claim again.

Dated the 20th November, 2009.

ROSE DETHO, Director, Deposit Protection Fund Board.

## <span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13156</span>
## THE ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT AND CO-ORDINATION ACT

(No. 8 of 1999)

## THE NATIONAL ENVIRONMENT MANAGEMENT AUTHORITY

## ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT STUDY REPORT FOR THE PROPOSED SEWER LINE DIVERSION OF THE EPZA SEWER LINE LOCATED BETWEEN PLOT NUMBERS: LR. 337/976, LR.337/1074 AND LR 337/2719 IN ATHI RIVER

## INVITATION OF PUBLIC COMMENTS

PURSUANT to regulation 21 of Environmental (Impact Assessment and Audit) Regulations, the National Environment Management  Authority  (NEMA)  has  received  an  Environmental Impact  Assessment  Study  Report  for  the  implementation  of  the Proposed Sewer Line Diversion of the Epza Sewer Line.

The proponent intends to create a sewage diversion of around 110 meters  for  its  factory  expansion  project  on  No.  LR.  337/2719.  The diversion  is  to  provide  space  for  the  factory  expansion.  The  site  is located  in  Athi  River  in  Mavoko  Municipality.  The  site  is  located between Plot Numbers: 337/976, 337/1074 337/2719.

The  project  anticipates  the  following  impacts  and  mitigation measures:

Possible Impacts

## Mitigation Measures

Location

Trenching

Foundations

Removing Water

-  Ascertain the location of all the water pipes, electrical installation and other possible interferences within the area of sewer construction.
-  Elevations  should  be  taken  at  intervals  in case of change of gradient.
-  Bench marks should be placed at convenient intervals for use during construction.
-  A specially equipped tractor will be required for this section and properly trained staff by the contractor
-  A  suitable  bedding  for  the  sewer  concrete pipes will be required and they should maintain the necessary grade.
-  Acceptable  grading  as  per  the  consultants expert should be provided
-  If  rock is present it should be removed to a depth of 4 to 6 inches below the bottom of the pipes' placement. if the soil is soft it will have to be stabilized with a packed layer of gravel or broken rock
-  Frequently the trench will collect water especially because we are in the rainy season
-  The  sewer  will  have  to  be  layed  from  the lowest part of the line to permit the water to flow away  from the completed sections centrifugal  pumps  will  be  required    to  be used for dewatering the trench.

Placing the concrete pipes

Provision for Factory Connections

Backfilling

Inspection

Measuring Infiltration

Record Keeping

-  For muddy material a diaphragm pump will be required.
-  For wet sections well points will be used or a  drain  with  open  joints    and  bedded  with gravel built underneath the sewer to remove the water.
-  The concrete pipes will have to be placed in their  exact  positions,  the  elevation  of  the pipes  will  be  checked  and  if  correct  a  joint will be made.
-  Where an immediate connection is not made,  a  vitrified  -  clay  will  have  to  be connected  to the branch  bell to prevent entrance of dirt or ground water.
-  Branches  or  slants,  for  factory  connections must be installed at the proper locations and with the stubs pointing to the correct side of the location.
-  The position decided on, may be marked  by a  stake  just  in  advance  of  concrete  pipe laying.
-  Because of the current construction activities  in  the  area,  the  need  for  a  firm backfill  will  be  required  because  of  the traffic issue
-  Compaction will be required during backfill with sand or gravel backfill.
-  Careful, skilled and continuous inspection of every  phase  of  sewer  construction  will  be required
-  Inspection will include examining each section  of  the  concrete  pipe  to  make  sure that it is unbroken and usable, checking the position  of  the  pipes  in  the  trench  for  line and  grade,  watching  the  forming  of  the joints, requiring proper bedding and backfill placement,  determine  the  need  for  trench drainage  to  ensure  that  good  work  can  be done, grade boards and gradient lines should be checked frequently for accuracy.
-  As soon as each section is completed, tests should be conducted to determine the level of infiltration or leakage into the sewer.
-  An exfiltration test will be required.
-  Because sewers are buried after construction careful records will be required during construction.
-  The  records  should  show  the  location  and size and the starting and ending points.

The full report of the proposed project is available for inspection during working hours at:

- (a) The  Director-General,  National  Environment  Management Authority, Popo Road, off Mombasa Road, P.O. Box 6783900200, Nairobi.
- (b) The  Permanent  Secretary,  Ministry  of  Environment  and Natural Resources, National Hospital Insurance Fund Building, Community, 4th Floor, P.O. Box 30521, Nairobi.
- (c) Provincial Director of Environment, Nairobi Province.
- (d) District Environment Officer, Nairobi West District.

The National Environment Management Authority invites members  of  the  public  to  submit  oral  or  written  comments  within thirty  (30)  days  from  the  date  of  publication  of  this  notice  to  the Director-General,  National  Environment  Management  Authority,  to assist the authority in the approval process of the project.

Dated the 12th November, 2009.

B. M. LANGWEN, for Director-General,

National Environment Management Authority.

<span style="background-color:#fff3cd;color:#1a1a1a;padding:0.15em 0.35em;border-radius:3px;font-weight:600;">GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13157</span>
## THE ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT AND CO-ORDINATION ACT

## (No. 8 of 1999)

## THE NATIONAL ENVIRONMENT MANAGEMENT AUTHORITY

ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT STUDY REPORT FOR THE PROPOSED NATIONAL CO-OPERATIVE HOUSING UNION (NACHU) PRESTIGE HOUSING SCHEME ON L.R. No. 23405 MAVOKO MUNICIPAL COUNCIL

## INVITATION OF PUBLIC COMMENTS

PURSUANT to regulation 21 of environmental (Impact Assessment and Audit) Regulations, the National Environment Management  Authority  (NEMA)  has  received  an  Environmental Impact  Assessment  Study  Report  for  the  implementation  of  the proposed  National  Co-operative  Housing  Union  (NACHU)  prestige Housing Scheme.

The  proposed  project  will  comprise  of  Type  A  semi  detached luxury  masionettes  housed on 70 No. plots of  minimum size 21.0 x 8.5m, each maisonnette is to have a plinth area of 100m². The second proposal will have Type B and will be composed of flats planned and arranged in 10 No. Each block is to accommodate 16 No. flats with a plinth area of 102.0m² per flat. The proposed project will be located on L.R. No. 23405 Mavoko Municipal Council.

The  project  anticipates  the  following  impacts  and  mitigation measures:

Possible Impacts

Mitigation Measures

Soil

Water Resources

Air and Noise pollution

-  Excavating only necessary areas.
-  Containment of soil heaps to prevent. erosion  caused  by  runoffs,  wind  and  from machinery.
-  Reduce the use of heavy machinery whenever possible.
-  Use  of  light  machinery  at  the  site  during construction process.
-  Leaving  trees  outside  designated  areas  of construction activities.
-  Excavating only construction areas.
-  Construction of drainage systems.
-  Prevention  of  pollution  during  construction activities to  minimize effects that may arise during surface runoffs.
-  Prevention  of  any  pollution  resulting  from construction activities.
-  Instituting water savings strategies to minimize water use.
-  Construction of drainage channels to ensure waste water handling.
-  Ensure reuse of waste water by sprinkling at the site to reduce excessive dust.
-  Construction of leak proof drains.
-  Instituting water saving strategies/practices.
-  Landscaping of the construction site.
-  Limiting construction traffic  movement and operation to efficient and necessary activities
-  Minimizing  transportation  activities  to  day time only
-  Routine  maintenance  of  vehicles  and  other machinery  to  be  used  during  construction process
-  Erection of buffer fence to retain most of the noise to the construction site

Visual Intrusion

Solid Waste

Occupational Health and safety

Effluent discharge

Public  nuisance  in form of smoke, smell and visual intrusion

-  The  road  leading  to  the  site  be  sprinkled with water to mitigate excessive dust emission
-  Sensitize construction drivers and machinery operators  to  switch  off  engines  when  not being used.
-  Limiting  construction  activities  to  day  time only
-  Regular serving of construction and transport  machinery  to  ensure  that  they  are in  good  working  condition  and  to  reduce emissions
-  Use of commercial bill boards to keep construction activities out of sight from immediate neighborhood.
-  Fencing out the construction site.
-  Landscaping and gardening to restore biodiversity  and  aesthetic  properties  of  the project site.
-  Waste minimization by avoiding unsustainable construction practices.
-  Sorting of waste.
-  Provision of dust bins to hold waste before disposal.
-  Reuse  where  possible  or  sale  to  authorized waste handlers/collectors.
-  Workers training on safety.
-  Risk analysis for all activities, materials and equipment.
-  Provision of protective clothing.
-  Emergency response plan.
-  Need for firefighting equipment to be made available on site.
-  Inclusion of fire exit route.
-  Effluent discharge shall be channeled to the main sewer line that serves the area.
-  All  effluent  to  meet  NEMA  standards  for discharge to a sewer line.
-  Provision  of  adequate  spatial  conditions  in the  project  design  to  avoid  congestion  and related public health and social problems.
-  Provision of trade opportunities for residents and surrounding community.
-  Construction of spacious driveways and walk ways.

The full report of the proposed project is available for inspection during working hours at:

- (a) The Director-General, National Environment Management Authority,  Popo  Road,  off  Mombasa  Road,  P.O.  Box 67839-00200, Nairobi.
- (b) The  Permanent  Secretary,  Ministry  of  Environment  and Natural Resources, National Hospital Insurance Fund Building, Community, 4th Floor, P.O. Box 30521, Nairobi.
- (c) Provincial Director of Environment, Eastern  Province.
- (d) District Environment Officer, Machakos District.

The National Environment Management Authority invites members  of  the  public  to  submit  oral  or  written  comments  within thirty  (30)  days  from  the  date  of  publication  of  this  notice  to  the Director-General,  National  Environment  Management  Authority,  to assist the authority in the approval process of the project.

Dated the 9th November, 2009.

B. M. LANGWEN, for Director-General,

National Environment Management Authority.

## GAZETTE NOTICE NO.13159

## THE ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT AND CO-ORDINATION ACT

(No. 8 of 1999)

## THE NATIONAL ENVIRONMENT MANAGEMENT AUTHORITY

## ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT STUDY REPORT FOR THE PROPOSED DEVELOPMENT OF A HOUSING ESTATE ON L.R. NO. 10426 /36, 37, 38 &amp; 39, MAVOKO MUNICIPALITY, MACHAKOS DISTRICT

## INVITATION OF PUBLIC COMMENTS

PURSUANT to regulation 21 of Environmental (Impact Assessment and Audit) Regulations, the National Environment Management  Authority  (NEMA)  has  received  an  Environmental Impact  Assessment  Study  Report  for  the  implementation  of  the Proposed Development of a Housing Estate on L.R. No. 10426 /36, 37, 38 &amp; 39, Mavoko Municipality.

The  proponent  intends  to  put  up  a  housing  estate  comprising  a total  of  262  low  cost  bungalows  of  two  and  three  bedrooms,  3  No. Plots have been set aside for sale to commercial developers (to bring commercial outlets closer to the estate) using regulated designs while 2 No. Plots have been set aside for development of a kindergarten.

The proposed development site comprises four plots registered as L.R.  Nos.  10426/36,  37,  38  &amp;  39  and  is  located  outside  Athi  River town in Machakos District. The site lies about 0.7 km off Mombasa Road, opposite Athi River Steel Plant Limited.

The  project  anticipates  the  following  impacts  and  mitigation measures:

## Possible Impacts

## Mitigation Measures

Air pollution, dust generation and noise pollution

-  Spray water during construction work.
-  Control speed and movements of construction  vehicles  noting  that  access  to project site is off a busy highway.
-  Use of low-sulphur diesel for dieseloperated machinery.
-  Use  of  appropriate  PPE    by  construction workers.
-  No  unnecessary hooting by project and residents vehicles.
-  Restriction  of  construction  activities  to  day time.
-  Use of equipment designed with noise control elements.

Clearing of vegetation

Generation of solid waste

Increased demand for water and electriticy

Increased demand for electricity

Occupational health and safety risks

Fire hazards and accidents

-  Temporarily  fencing  off  noisy  machinery such as vibrators.
-  Planting of ornamental trees along perimeter fence and within site.
-  Planting of grassed lawns.
-  Establishment of flower gardens within project project site.
-  No disturbance to areas not affected by the project so as to minimise impacts on environment.
-  Re-use of construction debris and other wastes
-  Proper  containment  and  disposal  of  solid waste at all project phases
-  Contracting  a  licensed  waste  collection  and disposal company
-  Awareness  raising  on  proper  solid  waste disposal
-  Re-use of timber off-cuts and wooden supports for fuel
-  Waste to be properly segregated and separated to facilitate re-use.
-  Conservation (wise use) of water.
-  Provision of adequate water storage facilities.
-  Installation of rainwater harvesting structures.
-  Re-use of water where possible.
-  Install water conserving taps.
-  Use of energy saving bulbs within the houses
-  Inclusion of a solar water heating &amp; lighting systems to reduce on use of electricity
-  Make use of natural lighting in the houses
-  Energy conservation measures to be practised
-  Use of suitable personal protective equipment (PPE).
-  Insurance of all workers.
-  Site to be sprinkled with water to minimize dust.
-  Use of stable ladders and other climbing/support structures.
-  Sensitise workers on construction safety measures.
-  Cleanliness and organisation at the construction site.
-  Fencing  or  covering  of  risky  areas  such  as deep pits.
-  Safety signage.
-  Use of  permit-to-work  authorizers  for  risky jobs.
-  Engagement of skilled labourers.
-  Food handlers to be monitored for hygienic practises.
-  Acquire fire fighting equipment.
-  Sensitise workers on fire safety.

Security

-  No storage of inflammables at site.
-  Keep well stocked first aid box.
-  Proper handling and use of tools and machinery.
-  Have a trained first aider on sit.e
-  Adequate road warning signs to traffic regulations.
-  Erection of speed bumps.
-  Guarding  of  site  and  estate  by  a  reputable security firm.
-  Constant site patrol.
-  Adequate screening of visitors to the site &amp; estate.
-  Collaboration with existing security machinery
-  Partnership  with  neighbours  and  police  in community policing.
-  Keep a record of visitors to the construction site and estate.

The full report of the proposed project is available for inspection during working hours at:

- (a) The Director-General, National Environment Management Authority,  Popo  Road,  off  Mombasa  Road,  P.O.  Box 67839-00200, Nairobi.
- (b) The  Permanent  Secretary,  Ministry  of  Environment  and Natural Resources, National Hospital Insurance Fund Building, Community, 4th Floor, P.O. Box 30521, Nairobi.
- (c) Provincial Director of Environment, Eastern Province.
- (d) District Environment Officer, Machakos District.

The National Environment Management Authority invites members  of  the  public  to  submit  oral  or  written  comments  within thirty  (30)  days  from  the  date  of  publication  of  this  notice  to  the Director-General,  National  Environment  Management  Authority,  to assist the authority in the approval process of the project.

Dated the 11th November, 2009.

B. M. LANGWEN, for Director-General,

National Environment Management Authority.

## CHANGE OF NAME

NOTICE is given that by a deed poll dated 28th September, 2009, duly executed and registered in the Registry of Documents at Nairobi, as  presentation  No.  2238,  in  Volume  DI,  Folio  217/2757,  File  No. MMIX, by our client, Kimmy Njeri Henderson, of P.O. Box 194900100, Nairobi in the Republic of Kenya, formerly known as Teresia Nyambura Njeri,  formally  and  absolutely  renounced  and  abandoned the  use  of  her  former  name  Teresia  Nyambura  Njeri,  and  in  lieu thereof assumed and adopted the name Kimmy Njeri Henderson, for all  purposes  and  authorizes  and  requests  all  persons  at  all  times  to designate,  describe  and  address  her  by  her  assumed  name  Kimmy Njeri Henderson only.

Dated the 28th September, 2009.

MAANZO &amp; COMPANY ADVOCATES, Advocates for Kimmy Njeri Henderson, formerly known as Teresia Nyambura Njeri.

## IMPORTANT NOTICE TO SUBSCRIBERS TO THE KENYA GAZETTE

THE following notes are for the guidance of persons submitting 'copy' for inclusion in the Kenya Gazette, Supplement , etc.:

- (1) The Kenya Gazette contains Notices of a general nature which do not affect  legislation.  They  are,  therefore,  submitted  to  the  Government Printer directly.
- (2) Legislative  Supplement contains  Rules  and  Regulations  which  are issued  by  the  Central  Government.  Because  of  this,  they  must  be submitted  to  the  Government  Printer  through  the  office  of  the Attorney-General.
- (3) Bill  Supplement contains  Bills  which  are  for  introduction  in  the National Assembly.
- (4) Act Supplement contains Acts passed by the National Assembly.

All 'copy' submitted for publication should be prepared on one side of an A4  sheet  no  matter  how  small  the  Notice  is,  each  page  being  numbered  and should be typewritten with double spacing. Copy should be clear, legible and contain no alterations.

Particular attention should be paid to the following points:

- (i) Signature must be supported by rubber-stamping or typing the name of the signatory in capital letters.
- (ii) Dates must be correct and filled in where necessary.
- (iii) Care  should  be  taken  to  ensure  that  all  headings  to  Notices  and references to legislation are up to date and conform with the Revised Edition of the Laws of Kenya.

EXTRACT FROM THE CODE OF REGULATIONS, SECTION D-

## Kenya Gazette

'D  34.  (1)  Communications  for  the Kenya  Gazette should  reach  the Government  Printer  not  later  than  9  a.m.  on  Friday  of  the  week  before publication is desired. The Government Printer will not publish communications received after that hour until the next subsequent issue of the Gazette.

- (2) Ministries will be required to pay for the Kenya Gazette and to meet the cost of advertising in it.

It  is  emphasized that these notes are for guidance only, but it is requested that  persons  submitting  copy  for  publication  first  satisfy  themselves  that  such copy is complete in every respect.
